The problem is that we can not test the speed except by reflection. It takes 2.56 seconds to bounce a beam off the moon and have it returned. We assume it took the same time going to the moon (1.28 sec) as returning from it. We have zero evidence that it's the same in both directions except that it's convenient to assume.   It could be that it took 2.55 seconds to leave the earth's stronger gravity well and only 0.01 seconds to return. We have no way to test if this is true or false.  This would mean that every source of light traveling out of a stronger gravity well, eg. the sun, would slow down the travel time and appear further away than it really is. It might take 400 seconds to reach earth as it climbs out of the stronger gravity but may take only 100 seconds to return. Again, we've no way to test this as all calibration of probes are based on the time we're trying to measure.

"In May and November, the Earth is moving at "right angles" to the line to Algol. During this time we see minima happening regularly at their 2.867321 day intervals. However, during August, the Earth is rapidly moving towards Algol at about 107,229 km/hr as explained on my¬†How Fast Are We Moving?¬†page. (The Earth moves approximately 202 times its own size in one day.) So in 2.867321 days the Earth moves about 7,379,039 km closer to Algol. _But the varying light from Algol doesn't know this - its light waves left Algol 93 years ago and are travelling at a constant speed._ The result - we "catch a bunch of minima early" during August as shown on Chart 2. Exactly the opposite happens during February - the Earth is moving away from Algol that fast and it takes longer for the group of minima to reach us so we see them taking longer between events. How long? 7,379,039 km divided by the speed of light 299,792.458 km/sec is 24.61382 seconds.  So in May and November when we are not moving towards or away from Algol - the period seems constant. It is our rapid movement towards or away from the events in August and February that causes the timing differences."  I assume that light is passing the earth at c when the earth isn't moving towards or away from Algol.  In February the earth is moving away from Algol and the time between the eclipses is 2.8675875347 days and the light is passing the earth at 186,265 mi/sec.  In May and November the earth is not moving towards or away from Algol and the time between eclipses is 2.867321 days and the light is passing the earth at 186,282 mi/sec.  In August the earth is moving towards Algol and the time between eclipses is 2.8670608912 days and the light is passing the earth at 186,299 mi/sec.

The medium through which EM waves travel permits only one maximum and minimum speed for EM waves. If it appears that the EM wave goes at a slower speed it is because the medium is to ‚Äúblame‚Äù.  Light travels inside quantum fields or threads that have standing waves stretching through them.  These standing waves contain a certain energy(wavelength, frequency and amplitude).  Gravity bunches up (compresses) the standing waves into one with higher amplitude and sorter wavelength.  The EM wave rides piggy back on the standing wave and has to travel a greater distance to get  around large bodies of mater, appearing to slow down.  Greater distance, same speed means more time to get past matter or out of gravity wells.

The speed of light is not a constant speed as once thought, and this has now been proved by Electrodynamic theory and by Experiments done by many independent researchers. The results clearly show that light propagates instantaneously when it is created by a source, and reduces to approximately the speed of light in the farfield, about one wavelength from the source, and never becomes equal to exactly c. This corresponds the phase speed, group speed, and information speed. Any theory assuming the speed of light is a constant, such as Special Relativity and General Relativity are wrong, and it has implications to Quantum theories as well. So this fact about the speed of light affects all of Modern Physics. Often it is stated that Relativity has been verified by so many experiments, how can it be wrong. Well no experiment can prove a theory, and can only provide evidence that a theory is correct. But one experiment can absolutely disprove a theory,  and the new speed of light experiments proving the speed of light is not a constant is such a proof. So what does it mean? Well a derivation of Relativity using instantaneous nearfield light yields Galilean Relativity. This can easily seen by inserting c=infinity into the Lorentz Transform, yielding the Galilean Transform, where time is the same in all inertial frames. So a moving object observed with instantaneous nearfield light will yield no Relativistic effects, whereas by changing the frequency of the light such that farfield light is used will observe Relativistic effects. But since time and space are real and independent of the frequency of light used to measure its effects, then one must conclude the effects of Relativity are just an optical illusion.  Since General Relativity is based on Special Relativity, then it has the same problem. A better theory of Gravity is Gravitoelectromagnetism which assumes gravity can be mathematically described by 4 Maxwell equations, similar to to those of electromagnetic theory. It is well known that General Relativity reduces to Gravitoelectromagnetism for weak fields, which is all that we observe. Using this theory, analysis of an oscillating mass yields a wave equation set equal to a source term. Analysis of this equation shows that the phase speed, group speed, and information speed are instantaneous in the nearfield and reduce to the speed of light in the farfield. This theory then accounts for all the observed gravitational effects including instantaneous nearfield and the speed of light farfield. The main difference is that this theory is a field theory, and not a geometrical theory like General Relativity. Because it is a field theory, Gravity can be then be quantized as the Graviton.  Lastly it should be mentioned that this research shows that the Pilot Wave interpretation of Quantum Mechanics can no longer be criticized for requiring instantaneous interaction of the pilot wave, thereby violating Relativity.  It should also be noted that nearfield electromagnetic fields can be explained by quantum mechanics using the Pilot Wave interpretation of quantum mechanics and the Heisenberg uncertainty principle (HUP), where Œîx and Œîp are interpreted as averages, and not the uncertainty in the values as in other interpretations of quantum mechanics. So in HUP: Œîx Œîp = h, where Œîp=mŒîv, and m is an effective mass due to momentum, thus HUP becomes: Œîx Œîv = h/m.  In the nearfield where the field is created, Œîx=0, therefore Œîv=infinity. In the farfield, HUP: Œîx Œîp = h, where p = h/Œª. HUP then becomes: Œîx  h/Œª = h, or Œîx=Œª. Also in the farfield HUP becomes: ŒªmŒîv=h, thus Œîv=h/(mŒª). Since p=h/Œª, then Œîv=p/m. Also since p=mc, then Œîv=c. So in summary, in the nearfield Œîv=infinity, and in the farfield  Œîv=c, where Œîv is the average velocity of the photon according to Pilot Wave theory. Consequently the Pilot wave interpretation should become the preferred interpretation of Quantum Mechanics. It should also be noted that this argument can be applied to all fields, including the graviton. Hence all fields should exhibit instantaneous nearfield and speed c farfield behavior, and this can explain the non-local effects observed in quantum entangled particles.  *YouTube presentation of above arguments: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=sePdJ7vSQvQ&t=0s   *More extensive paper for the above arguments: William D. Walker and Dag Stranneby, A New Interpretation of Relativity, 2023: http://vixra.org/abs/2309.0145  *Electromagnetic pulse experiment paper: https://www.techrxiv.org/doi/full/10.36227/techrxiv.170862178.82175798/v1  Dr. William Walker - PhD in physics from ETH Zurich, 1997

Experiment proves information can propagate instantaneously across space ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ We present an experiment that proves conclusively that information can be propagated nearly instantaneously across space, in the nearfield of an electromagnetic pulse. The experiment consists of a  ~30kV high voltage spark generator creating an electromagnetic pulse that propagated 1.5m to a detector. The leading edge of the transmitted pulse and the leading edge of the detected pulse were then compared using an oscilloscope and no time delay within the capability of the scope was observed, where 5ns is predicted if it had propagated at the light speed. The maximum uncertainty in the measurement was 1ns due to noise in the electronics. Since a pulse is digital information. This experiment proves information can be transmitted across space nearly instantaneously. The results is perfectly predicted by Maxwell equations, which yield a wave equation set equal to a source term. Analysis of this equation shows that the phase speed, group speed, and information speed are instantaneous in the nearfield and reduce to the speed of light in the farfield. Below is a link to see a preprint of the paper. We are currently looking for a journal for peer review and publication. The impact of this discovery has implications in both engineering and the foundations of modern physics. The result is completely incompatible with Relativity. Instantaneous signals invalidate Relativity of Simultaneity in all inertial frames and can be used to synchronize all their clocks. In addition, a derivation of Relativity using instantaneous electromagnetic fields (light) yields Galilean Relativity, where time is the same in all inertial frames of reference, and there is no speed limit for mass, fields, and, even light. This can be easily be seen by inserting c=infinity into the Lorentz Transform, yielding the Galilean Transform. This means that if a moving object is observed with farfield speed c light, then Relativistic effects will be observed. But the effects are not real and can be proved by simply changing the frequency of the light, such that instantaneous nearfield light is used, causing the Relativistic effects to disappear. This then proves that the effects of Relativity are just an optical illusion. Since General Relativity is based on Special Relativity, then it has the same problem. A better theory of Gravity is Gravitoelectromagnetism which assumes gravity can be mathematically described by 4 Maxwell equations, similar to to those of electromagnetic theory. It is well known that General Relativity reduces to Gravitoelectromagnetism for weak fields, which is all that we observe. Using this theory, analysis of an oscillating mass yields a wave equation set equal to a source term. Analysis of this equation shows that the phase speed, group speed, and information speed are instantaneous in the nearfield and reduce to the speed of light in the farfield. This theory then accounts for all the observed gravitational effects including instantaneous nearfield and the speed of light farfield. The main difference is that this theory is a field theory, and not a geometrical theory like General Relativity. Because it is a field theory, Gravity can be then be quantized as the Graviton. Lastly it should be mentioned that this research shows that the Pilot Wave interpretation of Quantum Mechanics can no longer be criticized for requiring instantaneous interaction of the pilot wave, thereby violating Relativity. Consequently the Pilot wave interpretation should become the preferred interpretation of Quantum Mechanics due to its deterministic simplicity. I love your vids.  It's worth noting, though, that as far as I understand (and I'll admit it's possible that I'm mistaken, as I am not an expert, but I'd love to see a vid from you guys on this), it's only the two-way speed of light (meaning light making a round trip, such as bouncing off a mirror and back again) that has been confirmed to be invariant, as there isn't a way to measure the one-way speed of light.  Einstein even had to define the speed of light in his equations in terms of the two-way speed of light as a result, and the speed of light traveling slower in one direction and faster in the opposite direction is consistent with the math of relativity.   The one-way speed of light being constant is simply a mathematical convention, not a necessity.  It's not (currently at least) verifiable one way or the other since the math is consistent and works out the same regardless of whether the one-way speed is constant or if light moves faster in one direction than another.

Would it not stand to reason that light moves at a constant speed relative to it's source? I mean it adheres to gravitational forces like traditional mass objects by bending around massive gravitational bodies or even to the point of being turned around and drawn into their gravitational wells entirely.   For example since each galaxy is moving away from each other if you look far enough away at a galaxy moving away from our own at half the speed of light relative to us and it's own light is moving towards us at a speed relative to it's source then the light we recieve would be moving at half the speed of light relative to us. It would also mean that our observations of that galaxy would be observed at half the speed that it's actually happened in that galaxy. We would essentially be observing further and further galaxies at progressively slower and slower speeds relative to the distance and speed of separation between us. And the further away a galaxy becomes the closer it becomes to the speed of light relative to us and eventually it's moving away from us faster than the speed of light. Hence why we cannot see galaxies that are too far away. Light essentially crosses a threashold where it moves slower towards us until it stops and then moves away from us even though relative to it's source it's moving towards us.  Could this then be observed by observing how much light bends around a gravitational mass such as a planet? For example compare the amount light from say the nearest star bends around a planet to say the amount light from a galaxy halfway to the edge of the observable universe. Since objects moving slower past a gravitational mass curves more around that mass we'd be able to observe whether or not light from further away curves more around that object than light coming from a closer source.  I'm sure smarter people than me have tested this theory of course. But I'd love to know what the result of such an experiment would be.

1:13 "This same axiom is also fundamental to general relativity..."  PATENTLY FALSE. General relativity invalidates it in anything but flat spacetime (hint: there's no such thing as flat spacetime in the real world)  Here's 5 Different quotes from Einstein REJECTING the validity of constancy:  ‚ÄúHowever, the writer of these lines is of the opinion that the theory of relativity is still in need of generalization, in the sense that the principle of the constancy of the velocity of light is to be abandoned‚Äù.  ‚ÄúThe theory presently called "the theory of relativity" is based on the assumption that there are somehow preexisting "privileged" reference systems K with respect to which the laws of nature take on an especially simple form, even though one raises in vain the question of what could bring about the privilegings of these reference systems K as compared with other (e.g.,"rotating") reference systems K'. This constitutes, in my opinion, a serious deficiency of this theory. These privileged reference systems are postulated as those with respect to which the principle of the constancy of the velocity of light in a vacuum is to be valid. There can be no doubt that this principle is of far-reaching significance; and yet, I cannot believe in its exact validity. It seems to me unbelievable that the course of any process (e.g., that of the propagation of light in a vacuum) could be conceived of as independent of all other events in the world. But whatever one may think of such arguments, it is in any case interesting to pose the question: To what extent is it possible to build a theory of relativity that does not have the constancy of the velocity of light as its foundation? [..] In the case where we drop the postulate of the constancy of the velocity of light, there exists, a priori, no privileged coordinate systems.‚Äù  ‚Äî clarifying the quote above, he's saying removing light speed constancy resolves the problematic issues and fixes the "serious deficiency" The ‚Äúprivileged‚Äù systems he refers to are FLAT spacetime ‚Äî  ‚ÄúOn the other hand, the empirical fact that all bodies fall equally fast in a gravitational field suggests the idea that physical processes occur in exactly the same way in a gravitational field as they do relative to an accelerated reference system (equivalence hypothesis). Having taken this idea as a basis, I arrived at the result that the velocity of light is not to be regarded as independent of the gravitational potential. Thus, the principle of the constancy of the velocity of light is incompatible with the equivalence hypothesis; for this reason, the theory of relativity in the narrower sense cannot be brought into agreement with the latter. In this way I was led to view the theory of relativity in the narrower sense as valid only for regions within which there are no noticeable differences in the gravitational potential.‚Äù  ‚ÄúIn the second place our result shows that, according to the general theory of relativity, the law of the constancy of the velocity of light in vacuo, which constitutes one of the two fundamental assumptions in the special theory of relativity and to which we have already frequently referred, cannot claim any unlimited validity‚Äù.  ‚ÄúSecond, this consequence shows that the law of the constancy of the speed of light no longer holds, according to the general theory of relativity, in spaces that have gravitational fields. As a simple geometric consideration shows, the curvature of light rays occurs only in spaces where the speed of light is spatially variable. From this it follows that the entire conceptual system of the theory of special relativity can claim rigorous validity only for those space-time domains where gravitational fields (under appropriately chosen coordinate systems) are absent. The theory of special relativity, therefore, applies only to a limiting case that is nowhere precisely realized in the real world."  The Collected Papers of Albert Einstein, Volume 7: The Berlin Years: Writings, 1918-1921 (English translation supplement), p 140  12:12 "The basic self consistency of the universe and the causal ordering of events is -in short -  under Lorentz Invariance. Break it and it's pretty easy to come up with nonsensical scenarios in which different observers have irreconcilable disagreements about the outcomes of events"  FALSE. Then I added 170 illustrations, and then the criticisms changed to, interesting idea. In a nutshell, I believe there is background distortion in various quantities at locations throughout our universe. The early universe didn't have such distortion and consequently, a higher rate of light speed. It's this background distortion that knots up the speed of light. It's also a factor of time, so in many ways, it does not affect the speed of light, but it affects the speed of time light is traveling through.

If we consider the universe as a whole in terms of density, then maximum physical density would be defined by the singularity prior to the big bang. From that point onwards until our current observable time, the Universe to our understanding has expanded exponentially, which by nature would mean that density per physical volume has lessened at a comparable scale. This would directly explain the possibility of VSL through time (or not time per se, but unfolding of events). If light was perceived at a lower pace relative to the higher density of the Universe during singularity, it would mean light would be perceived as standstill since the density of the singularity is infinite / undefinable. And this matches with the fact that there can not exist time in a singularity since nothing can physically move, thus lightspeed can not be perceived as there is no relative point of observation.  Post big bang and the burst of the singularity, density of the Universe lessened, and speed of light could be perceived from relative points of view. Even though the speed of light technically may still be infinite, our ability to perceive it is defined by the density of the Universe around us, thus we do not perceive infinity but rather 299,792,458 m/s. However, that is only relative to our physical position in the expanding Universe, at this specific point in time. If we are to consider the Universe's expansion being exponential, that would mean that the closer to an event horizon (or the edge of the observable universe) we get, the more the perceivable speed of light would change. Likewise it would then be assumed that the perceived speed of light would be greater than 299,792,458 m/s the closer we get to the true center of the Universe and origin of the singularity expansion, since density here would be vastly greater than our location in the Milky Way galaxy. This would theoretically confirm VSL not just relative to time, but also relative to position of observation in the Universe. It would also mean that actual speed of light is infinite, but the density of the Universe from which we observe said light, will define how we observe it. We can also speculate that all observation of light depends on receiving a return signal to confirm that the light travelled to the intended destination. Say if we shine a light to a mirror on the moon, and then observe the return signal when we observe the light photon post reflection, what are we deducing? Are we deducing that the speed of light equals the time it took to observe its return? Or are we merely deducing how long it took us to obtain an observable return signal? The light could have gone the distance in an instant, but the observable pace may trail behind due to the density of the Universe through which the observation is being made, like an afterimage or light ghosting as I personally like to call it.  If we further consider that the density of the Universe is defined not by any matter (be it dark or normal or anti), but rather gravity itself, the natural attraction of all things observable -even the perception of light. Is light the photonic wave, or is that wave just the observable and interactive byproduct of what light is? Now we are going into full speculation, but it's interesting to ponder over.

Given the separate appearance of permittivity, I would disagree that fine structure depends on c.  Rather, the fine structure depends on the ratio of permeability to permittivity not its product.  It is easy to vary the product while keeping the ratio (and alpha) constant...  Just let u0=a u0' and e0=a e0'.  Then, c~1/a and alpha is constant.  This is true for an arbitrary function a(...) not zero... including a~10^{-20}.

EDIT: Re-wrote to be a bit more concise:   Prior to 2019, the meter, which is used to measure the speed of light, was defined using the distance from the equator to the north pole.  It was changed to instead be defined by the speed of light.  So, since 2019, the meter is defined by the speed of light, the speed of light is defined by the meter and the second, and the second is defined by the meter and the speed of light.  All three are circularly defined and treated as constants.  If any one of them changes, no one will ever know....

One thing that sometimes confuses me a little is the way the word "constant" gets used. For instance, the speed of light has to be invariant with respect to boosts, but it isn't necessary that it be constant over time. Energy in an isolated system is constant over time, but it certainly isn't invariant with respect to boosts. The Hubble constant is not invariant (in fact, it's only defined for one reference frame), nor is it remotely constant over time, but it is constant over space.  Maybe when we talk about "constants," we should be clear what we mean by that. Constant with respect to what?

I am intrigued that gravity waves have been measured to propagate at the same speed as that of light.  This is not an obvious result to have expected since light speed is determined by the more fundamental constants, the permeability and permittivity of the vacuum.  So, I ask this question: why should gravity waves give a hoot about the permeability and permittivity of the vacuum?  Some musing on this curiosity is that they are both traveling through an ether with a density that both observe.  But the Michelson-Morley experiment disproved the ether theory, didn't it?  Well, maybe not.  The experiment was a classical thought experiment and not a quantum mechanical one.  The vacuum "ether" is definitely a quantum mechanical beasty meaning that it would not have a velocity in any particular direction like a cumulonimbus cloud.  Its constituents are here at one moment and gone the next (the quantum soup of virtual particles).  Because the gravity wave is not accompanied by a moving mass, it must be the compression and relaxation of this quantum ether that we call space-time.  It does beg the question: has this density been the same since time zero (and I suppose before then?).  The follow-on question then turns to the nature of space-time.  Gravity is said to be a field with masses (and presumably anti-masses) always attracting, never repelling.  However. space-time may in places be of positive curvature (gravity would have to overcome this field effect before attractive acceleration would occur), negative curvature (that which would eventually give is the big crunch) or flat.  This idea separates (and marries) the notions of "gravity", "gravity waves" and space-time curvature.  What I'm hinting at is that dark energy may be the latter, a positive curvature field that gravity must first overcome before masses observe Newtonian or relativistic attraction.  In a universe teeming with symmetries, perhaps the universe's birth created negative curvature forcing a positive curvature at its boundaries and beyond so that the net field observed from beyond the universe retains flatness.    This would be a nice theory for explaining inflation (initial very high negative curvature induces very high positive curvature around it).  Inflation has always bothered me as a convenient hat trick with no explanation in physics.  Inflation ties into this "speed of light" question I think.

The scale factor, $a(t)$, can be interpreted as implying $c = c_0 \sqrt{a(t)}$. You wouldn't notice that change in the moment, but it should be possible to discern when comparing two times using the ruler of one of them. It's a bit like monetary inflation. A dollar is a dollar, but that dollar 20 years ago bought you twice as much as it does today.  Start with the usual metric $ds^2 = c^2d\tau^2 = cdt^2 - a(t) dx^2$. That's a normed split-complex number (or hyperbolic quaternion if dx is a 3-vector) of the form $cd\tau = |cdt + j \sqrt{a(t)} dx|$ where $j^2=1$. Now, divide both sides by $c$ and you get $d\tau = |dt + j \frac{\sqrt{a(t)}}{c}dx|$. You can then square that term and shove it in the definition of $j$ for a final form of $d\tau=|dt +jdx|$ where $j=\sqrt{\frac{a(t)}{c^2}}=\sqrt{c_0^{-2}}$. That term defines the relation between the two coefficients of the split-complex.  It's worth noting that GR also implies that $cd\tau\times dx$ is invariant regardless of relative velocity or gravity which includes expansion of the universe. It's not so obvious in Minkowski space-time as the manifold is infinite there but you can calculate the surface volume of the hypersphere in Euclidean space-time for any given time $t$ (since the big bang) and work out what $dt$ is relative to $dt_0$ at some time $t_0$. _This assumes the gravitational potential and velocity relative to the CMB is the same between the two points in time._ It's the same in Minkowski space-time between points on any two hyper-hyperbolic paraboloid surface volumes. It'd might make more sense to do this in terms of a Lorentz-like $\gamma(t)dt$ rather it being a different $dt$ since a second is always a second, just some are shorter or longer than others as if you are using a different unit system at different times.  Note, the equations would be easier to read if you copy this into a Markdown or LaTeX editor. Kind of a shame YT only has partial Markdown support. I replaced the $\mathrm{d}$ with $d$ so it's at least a little less cluttered but it's still a difference operator, not a separate variable. I would have replaced $\frac{a}{b}$ with $a/b$ but then I'd have to rearrange some equations in annoying ways to avoid ambiguity.

Ironically when scientists keep measuring the speed of light across years it changes speeds. But thats fine, all we have to do is base our units of measurement off of the currently measured speed of light, that way it always remains a constant.  So because of that across the years the length of a meter has changed. Now because we base the length of a meter off the speed of light the actual distance it changes is so miniscule that it doesnt actually matter when looking at any sort of terrestrial measurement. But just know that while the speed if light never changes, somehow light years get longer and shorter distance wise.  Remember kids, in science going the same speed does not mean going the same distance, just so we can proclaim something as a "universal constant".

The Monad (first emanation of God):  Once upon a time there was a vast and empty void. It was an endless expanse of nothingness, with no matter, energy, or even light.  But within this emptiness, there was a tiny spark. It was a singularity, a point of infinite density and temperature, where the laws of physics as we know them break down. And from this spark, the universe was born.  At the very beginning of time, the universe was incredibly small and hot. All the matter and energy that would one day form galaxies, stars, and planets was packed into a tiny, zero-dimensional space. This space was so small that it could hold just a few elementary particles, the building blocks of matter.  But even in this tiny space, something incredible was happening. The particles were held together by a powerful force, known as the Strong Nuclear Force. This force is responsible for binding the protons and neutrons in the nucleus of an atom, and without it, the particles would simply fly apart.  As the universe expanded and cooled, the particles began to combine to form atoms, molecules, and eventually, the first stars and galaxies. And yet, even as the universe grew and evolved, the Strong Nuclear Force continued to hold the particles together.  As scientists peered deeper into the structure of matter, they discovered that the particles themselves were made up of even smaller building blocks, known as quarks. And once again, the Strong Nuclear Force was there, binding the quarks together to form protons and neutrons.  The story of the Strong Nuclear Force is intimately connected to the story of our universe. It is the force that holds matter together, from the smallest particles to the largest structures in the cosmos. Without it, the universe as we know it could not exist.  And so, as we gaze up at the stars and ponder the mysteries of the universe, let us remember the tiny, zero-dimensional space that holds our quarks together with the Strong Nuclear Force, and the role it has played in shaping our cosmic history.

c is absolute (Einstein relativity) because Einstein refers to a relative moving observer towards or away of a light source who however (and here is the tricky part) is assumed sees the light already. The observer is already engulfed by the EM waves of this light! Similar to a swimmer inside a wavy sea. The propagation speed of the waves going towards or away from the observer does not change and is independent to the observer's velocity but only the frequency of the waves (Doppler effect) hitting the observer changes and therefore also vice versa the separation of the observer from the waves (wavelength) but the propagation speed of the waves remains the same absolute non-relative value c=Œªf. However, if the shooting light from a moving source has not yet reached the moving observer (swimmer) then the speed of light becomes relative to the observer's motion (Galilean relativity). Thus, the faster the observer moves towards the light source the less time will pass for the light reaching the observer. Therefore now the speed of light becomes relative and not absolute to the observer's motion and faster than c if the observer moves towards the light source and the light has not yet reached the observer.

The smoothie scenario can be observable to different observers in different ways. It isn't that you would observe the smoothie hitting the floor before it falls, but rather if you had two smoothies a distance apart that an observer dropping them would see them hitting the ground at the same time. Along a plane equidistant from both smoothies, they would land at the sane time. Another observer standing closer to one of the smoothies would see the closer one strike first while another observer standing closer to the second would see it strike first. There are two events occurring and three different ways to observe the order of these two events.  If we extend this concept to a significant distance between where these two events occur, other sides of the galaxy let's say, it is more recognizable. A locally observable event would take 2 million years to be observed on the other side of the galaxy and for the same reason it would take 2 million years for a local event on the other side to be observed the other way. Somewhere in the middle of the two events it would be seen to occur at the same time. Directly between, both events would be observered at 1 million years after the events, but there are regions where both events will be observered simultaneously 2 million years or more after they happened.  The point is that the order these events occur are observed to be different depending on where the observer is standing in relation. The effect of this dilation is probably better described as a field as information is distorted between all events over distances.  While this is occurring, I'll contend that time is slowing down as space expands. Just like moving the walls of the photon clock apart from one another, the fabric of space is expanding.  At the fringe of the observable Universe, light was moving at its fastest at the literal dawn of time, 300,000 km/s. More specifically information was exchanged at that rate. It isn't  a surprise that this is the rate we observe locally as well.  Where this is problematic is the shells which surround the big bang. The information exchanged between points on the expanding shells is transfered at the same rate, but as the shells expand outward from that epoch, the distance between adjoining locations will continue to spread apart and thus time will dilate and slow down. At the furthest, at what could only be described as the center of the observable Universe, time at the fringe will have effectively stopped. The nasty side effect of this being that what we can observe will effectively be imperceptible. There will be a redshift as that light smeared  on the horizon will be elongated and stretched, but the rate will appear to us the be the same with a different frequency.  So far I've been talking about space, but time is effected in the same way, rather it changes at the distance away from.the observer.  To complicate things further, the effect of dilation is occuring everywhere all at once, and so until we can place an observer half way between is and the fringe,  we will have no way to measure it. Locally it is the same and the difference could only be  observable with observers significnant distanced apart.

"It is absolutely necessary to insist that such a fundamental statement as the principle of covariance should be derived, if possible, from the simplest BASIC provisions. Einstein showed, and this is his great merit, that for this purpose it is enough to accept only the following electrodynamic position:   the speed of light does not depend on the motion of the source.   If the light source is a point, then in all cases the wave front is a sphere with a resting center. We will, as is customary, briefly call this provision the provision on the "constancy of the speed of light", although such a name may give rise to misunderstandings. The universal constancy of the speed of light in the void is out of the question already because the speed of light is constant only in Galilean reference frames. The independence of the speed of light from the motion of the source is preserved in the general theory of relativity." (Pauli, RT, paragraph 3, The postulate of the constancy of the speed of light).

Increasing the distance between the mirrors only works if you're doing so by expanding the space, not by moving the mirrors through space. If you double the distance by moving the mirrors twice as far apart in space, rather than by expanding space to twice the size, then your clock only counts a day as lasting 12 hours. If you do it by expanding the space, the clock still counts 24 hours, but an observer in a space where the expansion didn't happen would see 48 hours pass for your expanded patch of space.

The speed of light is derived from the vacuum permittivity constant and the magnetic constant. For the speed of light to vary, either one or both of these constants would need to vary. That would be easy to detect, I think.
If the speed of light is the same from all observers, then it's also the same from the perspective of light. That would mean that if two photons are travelling next to each other in the same direction, one photon would see the other photon move away from it at the speed of light. We don't observe this though, so the statement that the speed of light is the same for all observers, cannot be true.

Fun fact: you can treat the expansion of space as being a changing of the speed of light. In fact, in co-moving coordinates (a coordinate system that doesn't expand with space-time) that's exactly what it is. The FLRW metric is diag(-c^2, a(t)^2), where a(t) is the scale factor (it's defined to be 1 today, and smaller in the past). So in this coordinate system the distance a photon can travel is c / a(t). In this picture light gradually slows down, and eventually stops. We normally don't use this picture, though, instead saying that physical distances are expanding and c is constant. To keep alpha constant, you'd have to have other constants changing, too, and since c^2 = 1/(epsilon_0 * mu_0), epsilon_0 would naturally, also, change with time in such a way that keeps alpha constant.

Another intriguing solution to the causal connection of almost all matter in the early universe giving thermal equilibrium and then a period of seemingly faster than light expansion and then a slowing of that again, which would not violate the speed of causality, would be Stephen Wolfram's "The Wolfram Physics Project". This builds on his "New kind of science" looking at the universe as computation on a hypergraph. The short form is that in the very early universe, the fabric of space wasn't 3 dimensional but had a higher dimensionality. A regular mesh where all nodes have 6 neighbors makes a 3D lattice, while in the early universe the number may have been much higher, and so two points in space that today has coordinates very far apart may have been much fewer jumps away on the graph. The dimensionality of this hypergraph decreasing would also give the effect of expanding space (as the number of jumps between points increases). I haven't read that much on this physics project yet, but a few interesting things follow, like space could have a non-integer dimensionality, where at this point in time it just happens to be extremely close to 3 in most of the observable universe, but it could deviate some places, like in the vast emptiness between galactic clusters a lower dimensionality and potentially decreasing dimensionality would explain the perceived stretching of space there. Mass bending space-time (slowing) could also be explained by that maintaining the structure of space requires more computation when there is matter nearby, and so less computation available to propagate information through the graph. This will make more sense if you know about cellular automata and the game of life, and how patterns can self-replicate or propagate. Anyway, Stephen Wolfram has some fascinating podcast appearances with Lex Fridman that I highly recommend for those interested in hearing some hours on this.

Actually even in the framework of Special Relativity, the speed of light is constant only within an inertial reference frame; it does not remain constant in a non-inertial reference frame.  In a non-inertial reference frame with constant proper acceleration, also known as the Rindler coordinate, the speed of light depends on the location where the light beam is sent and could even become zero in certain cases. The region of spacetime where the speed of light is exactly zero is referred to as the Rindler horizon. This horizon serves as a boundary that the accelerated observer can never reach because the light beam cannot reach them.  This phenomenon arises because spacetime is hyperbolic, and at an appropriate distance, the asymptote can never intersect with a hyperbola. The hyperbola represents an accelerated worldline, while the asymptote represents a beam of light.  This also explains why light cannot escape a black hole, as the speed of light becomes zero at the event horizon, according to the Schwarzschild metric. In the Schwarzschild metric, the speed of light for a radial light beam is expressed as dr/dt = ¬±c(1-Rs/r), where "Rs" is the Schwarzschild radius.  Nevertheless, the speed of light at any given distance still depends on "c," which is why "c" remains fundamental in both special and general relativity.

This is related to one of your older videos but has anyone else found that rather than faster than light travel itself being a time travel paradox, instead the issue only arises when an observer is the accelerating reference frame and thus it would be more accurate to postulate that no observer may accelerate past the speed of light? Information, energy, etc. don't care that they arrived, from their perspective, before they left. For all outside reference frames, the object is only arriving prior to the light that would show its location; if light traveled from point A 1000 light years to point B, then someone at point B sent an instant message to point A, it would still arrive within a linear causality 1000 years after the event that prompted the message by emitting the light. If point A sent a message about a light speed event to point B, a return message could arrive 1000 years before the event hit point B but that would still be after the event was observed by point A. The issue arises when the accelerating reference frame carries an observer, because at light speed the reference frame will experience no time passing and beyond that the reference frame will experience arrival prior to departure, but that is subjective to the reference frame and thus is resolved by disallowing an observer to be within the reference frame. This also resolves things like the Alcubierre Drive, because the observers within that reference frame do not actually accelerate beyond light speed but instead warp space to travel larger distances with sub-light travel speeds, and outside reference frames would experience arrival of the reference frame before they observed the departure but still chronologically after the departure point observed the departure, evidenced by the fact that a return journey would have them arrive after the light had moved a certain distance thus showing that for the departure point, things happened in a linear time frame.

Space-time is an emergent property of the universe when one considers massive systems, which means composite systems. Elementary particles are massless, therefore they don't experience such things as space and time. Those things do not exist at an fundamental level. In this context, c is just a scaling paremeter. It's not a magic number, it's not a fundamental constant or whatever, it's just a scaling parameter that enables us to use two different unit systems to measure spacelike intervals and timelike intervals. This scaling parameter only exists in our maths, not in reality. It can therefore not vary as non-existing stuff do not have that possibility. If we observe someone traveling at the speed of light, they have total spacetime compression relative to us, appearing frozen in time and compressed to zero size.  So worded another way (and I forget where I heard this... possibly on this channel)    if we observe someone traveling at "c" they have zero velocity "through time", and    if we observe someone at rest, they have "c" velocity through time. Circular reasoning.  A meter is defined in terms of distance traveled in a unit of time at the speed of light.  The speed of light is defined as meters light travels in a unit of time.  With those definitions, we can't measure variations in the speed of light.  Physicists like cosmic inflation, but to my untrained eye, it looks like a fudge factor.  If gravity wells affect the speed of light... Then when the mass of the universe was extremely dense, we've got some recalculating to do. It would be nice to ditch circular definitions and look.
In my own, philosophically-motivated cosmology, I reckon time itself to literally be a path through the state-space of the universe, such that two neighboring moments in time literally are just two minimally-different possible states of the universe. Preferred direction through the state space, and so the arrow of time, is given by the anisometry of entropy. And yes, it follows that there are many equally real paths through this multidimensional time, that every moment has not only multiple futures but also multiple pasts, and yes I think this does relate to quantum mechanics and the many worlds interpretation thereof, but that's not what I came to talk about today. I came to talk about the topic of this video.  It follows directly from this that there is necessarily a constant rate of change in the universe. Since movement is a kind of change, there is thus a constant rate of movement... at least, unless the moving things are also changing in some other, internally confined, not externally kinetic way, since some "ticks of the cosmic clock" must be spent on performing those changes, instead of changes in overall position, i.e. movement. Thus any confined energy prevents things from moving at their normal, maximal rate; and conversely, the faster things move, the slower any internal processes within them must occur, because more "ticks of the cosmic clock" are being spent on changes in overall position, i.e. movement, rather than on those internal processes.  Not only does this give us inertial mass as the product of confined energy (mass-energy equivalence), but also any periodic process being used to measure time, be it a clock or a brain, will measure less time to occur while in faster motion. Meanwhile space, on this model, is reckoned as definitionally a measure of the (minimal) time it takes for a change to one part of the universe to affect a change in another part: that time is the distance between those parts of the universe. If a process being used to measure time is distorted, it follows directly that all measurements of distance in terms of that time will also be distorted. Et voila, special relativity: measures of space and time distort with motion to ensure that massless particles like photons (in a vacuum) always appear to move at a constant speed to all observers.  On this model, as you'll note above, energy works out to just be any changes occurring, and the conservation of energy thus follows directly from the constant rate of change. Thus it follows that in places where there is lots of energy, there is lots of change happening, even if it's all just internal change confined within a space, i.e. mass. Since the rate of change overall is constant, if there's already a lot of changes happening in an area, other changes will have to wait their turn, and so time will be measured to slow down in proximity to concentrations of mass-energy. This of course in turn requires that distances will be measured to distort in the proximity of mass-energy as well. Either of these distortions of space or time suffices to bend otherwise straight lines through spacetime toward the concentration of mass. Et voila, gravity qua general relativity as well.  For one last note: given that the arrow of time is toward more-entropic parts of the state space, and larger volumes have higher entropy potential, we would naturally expect to find space to increase in size over time, just at random, new tiny bits of space added in between others everywhere always, albeit at a rate, that has to compete with other changes happening, such that you would only really observe it in places very far away from concentrations of mass, like in the intergalactic voids, and the bigger and emptier the void, the greater the rate of expansion. So, there you go, dark energy too. But since there is now more space over which changes can occur, the rate of change per volume of space is diluted, so this expansion of space is also necessarily a dilation of time, or equivalently a change in the speed of light; they're all different aspects of the same phenomenon.

10:17 It isn't necessary to look in exotic places to disprove the idea that higher energy photons have greater speed. The energy of a photon is dependent on its frequency given by the simple and elegant equation E = hf. That means photons of different colors of light have different energies. If this hypothesis were true then we should measure different speeds of light for different colors of light, or more generally, for different frequencies of any electromagnetic wave, such as radio waves and gamma rays.  10:39 What mechanism would be responsible for this effect to only kick in a super high energies? Again, a judicious application of Occam's Razor should put these theories to rest.

So *technically* it is *possible* the actual speed that light travels could vary without changing the "C" constant. Since the "C" constant really just refers to how fast something can travel in the universe. We only call it the "speed of light" because light travels at that speed. Really, it's the speed at which radiation can propagate, light just being one form of that radiation. Gravity also travels at the speed of light. All of this is showing there is a disconnect between the "C" constant, and the "speed of light". The speed of light CAN VARY, but "C" must remain(as it's title of constant implies), constant. Thanks for this interesting video. The idea is super cool, it is part of a more general hypothesis that the physical constants might vary over time and space. For example, some scientists have suggested that the gravitational constant or the fine-structure constant might also change. Recently, a researcher named Rajendra Gupta has used this hypothesis to claim that our universe is 27 billion years old, not 13.7 billion and that the cosmological constant is not constant at all. His model is based on two old ideas: that the speed of light decreases as photons travel (tired light theory) and that the coupling constants evolve with time (Dirac‚Äôs hypothesis). if two atoms interact with each other at the speed of light there is very little gravity between them.   If you then have 100 atoms they each have to interact with every other one, so 100x100, and they have to do it at the speed of light. There will be a little more gravity. The more atoms are added, the more gravity appears.  It's as if the complex speed of light interactions needed to sustain larger and larger groups of atoms, the more latency is introduced and time has to compensate in order to keep the speed of causality constant from the reference frame of the atoms. Slowing time = curvature in spacetime.  It's like the frame rate of the universe slows in the presence of atoms all interacting with every other atom in order to maintain C. For anyone experiencing that drop in framerate there will be no perceivable difference, it's only when measuring it relative to the rest of the unvierse that the framerates differ.

General relativity and quantum mechanics will never be combined until we realize that they take place at different moments in time. Because causality has a speed limit (c) every point in space where you observe it from will be the closest to the present moment. When we look out into the universe, we see the past which is made of particles (GR). When we try to look at smaller and smaller sizes and distances, we are actually looking closer and closer to the present moment (QM). The wave property of particles appears when we start looking into the future of that particle. It is a probability wave because the future is probabilistic. Wave function collapse happens when we bring a particle into the present/past. GR is making measurements in the predictable past. QM is trying to make measurements of the probabilistic future.

Real relativity dictates this is impossible logically because multiple observers can have different frames of reference. Therefor, if two light beams are triggered in the same direction perfectly parallel, but one light source is already moving towards this direction, then the moving light source will be travelling faster than the one that isn't moving. But that's the thing about real relativity, entropy is local, not global, therefor there is no objective frame of reference, and therefor, all observations made from Earth and its vicinity are biased in their testing. We observe distant supernovas in the "past" because the light does not travel instantly. And therefor items that are moving perpendicularly from us billion of light "years" away from us are casting images to us that are actually deformed by the bending over distance of the light trajectory. The effect is akin to a fish eye lens and this is why JWST had to be adjusted because their calibration was entirely wrong for this concept, and I think what they did to patch it was actually reversing the concept that it can make us discover new things about light because now they're calibrated it to work according to past experiments we've ran successfully from the same point of reference. This is exactly the reason why gravity might actually be the collapse of extra dimensions rather than a directional force.
